FLUENT HOUR / PERFECT HOUR — REVISED CORE CURRICULUM (A1 → C2)
Now includes intuitive IDs and unique 'idea' anchors for every session and every phase.

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 001
Session Idea: Saying-I-M: navigate 'Saying "I'm Sorry" After a Mistake' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Saying "I'm Sorry" After a Mistake
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can say simple greetings and make very simple requests/apologies.
Context: You accidentally bump into someone or step on their foot in a crowded city street.
Correction: Helper will recast "No good" or "Bad me" to "I'm sorry" or "Excuse me."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 001.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Saying-I-M: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Automate the sound of an apology.
Human steps:

* Say "I'm sorry" ten times.
* Say "Excuse me" ten times.
* Practice "Are you okay?" three times.
AI helper script: I am a person on the street. Every time you say "I'm sorry," I will say "That's okay." We will do this fast to build your confidence in the sound.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 001.2
Phase Idea: Model Saying-I-M: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the rhythm of a quick apology and response.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Oh! I'm sorry."
* Helper says: "It's okay. No problem."
* Listen to the difference between "I'm sorry" (my fault) and "Excuse me" (move please).
* Repeat "It's okay" after the helper five times.
AI helper script: Model a three-step interaction. 1. Bump into person. 2. Say "I'm sorry." 3. Listen to "It's okay." Use big gestures to show the accident.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 001.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Saying-I-M: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Perform the apology in a "real" moment.
Human steps:

* Walk toward the helper and pretend to bump into them.
* Say "I'm sorry" immediately.
* Ask "Are you okay?"
* Repeat the simulation, but this time use "Excuse me" to get past them.
AI helper script: Act as a stranger. I am walking past you. When you bump me, I will look surprised. Wait for your apology. Say "No problem" or "I am fine."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 001.4
Phase Idea: Polish Saying-I-M: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Check the "softness" of the apology.
Human steps:

* Record: "I am sorry. Are you okay? Excuse me."
* Listen: Did you sound polite or angry?
* Write "Sorry" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to my recording. Recast the word "Sorry" if the vowel sound was too flat. Give me a "can-do" check for the apology.

Twists:

* You dropped the person's bag.
* You are in a very narrow hallway.
* The person is a child.
* The person is angry and says "Hey!"
* You are carrying a hot coffee.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 002
Session Idea: Asking-Price-Bus: navigate 'Asking the Price of a Bus Ticket' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking the Price of a Bus Ticket
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask simple questions about items and handle money.
Context: You are at a ticket window in a town bus station.
Correction: Helper will recast "Bus money?" to "How much is a ticket?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 002.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Price-Bus: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill the word "Ticket" and numbers.
Human steps:

* Say "Ticket" ten times.
* Say "One ticket, please" five times.
* Practice numbers 10, 20, 30.
AI helper script: I am a ticket seller. You ask "Ticket?" and I will give you a price. Repeat the price back to me.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 002.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Price-Bus: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Understand the question for price.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Hello. How much is one ticket?"
* Helper says: "It is five dollars."
* Helper says: "Here is five dollars. Thank you."
* Repeat the question "How much is one ticket?" three times.
AI helper script: Model the interaction slowly. Point to a sign that says "Price" while you speak. Use your hands to show the exchange of money.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 002.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Price-Bus: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Buy a ticket to a specific town.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper and say the town name (e.g., "London?").
* Ask "How much is a ticket?"
* Pretend to count money and pay.
* Repeat the simulation, but ask for "Two tickets."
AI helper script: Act as a bus ticket seller. I will ask for a price. Give me a number between 1 and 20. If I don't give you enough money, point and say "More."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 002.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Price-Bus: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on number clarity.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. One ticket to [Town], please. How much? Okay, thank you."
* Listen: Did the numbers sound clear?
* Write the price in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the town name if it was hard to understand. Give me a "can-do" check for the purchase.

Twists:

* The ticket window is closed.
* You need a ticket for "Tomorrow."
* The bus is full.
* You only have a credit card.
* The price is more than you have.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 003
Session Idea: Identifying-Yourself-Phone: navigate 'Identifying Yourself on the Phone' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Identifying Yourself on the Phone
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions about myself.
Context: You are calling a work office or a doctor and need to say who you are.
Correction: Helper will recast "I [Name]" to "This is [Name] calling."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 003.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Identifying-Yourself-Phone: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Automate the phone introduction.
Human steps:

* Say "Hello, this is [Your Name]" ten times.
* Say "Is [Name] there?" five times.
* Practice "One moment, please" three times.
AI helper script: I will pick up a "fake" phone and say "Hello?" You give me your name using the phrase. We will do this until you don't hesitate.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 003.2
Phase Idea: Model Identifying-Yourself-Phone: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the standard phone opening.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Hello, this is Maria."
* Helper says: "Who is calling, please?"
* Helper responds: "This is [Your Name]."
* Repeat the question "Who is calling?" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model a phone call. 1. Ring-ring. 2. Say hello. 3. Identify yourself. 4. Say who you want to talk to. Speak slowly into your hand like a phone.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 003.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Identifying-Yourself-Phone: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully start a phone call.
Human steps:

* Pretend to dial the helper.
* Greet them and state your name.
* Ask for a specific person (e.g., "Is the manager there?").
* Repeat the simulation, but this time "The manager" is not there.
AI helper script: Act as a receptionist. I will call you. Ask me my name if I forget to say it. Tell me "He is busy" to see how I respond.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 003.4
Phase Idea: Polish Identifying-Yourself-Phone: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "This is" structure.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. This is [Name]. Is Sam there? Thank you."
* Listen: Did you sound confident?
* Write "This is [Your Name]" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the phrase "This is" if it sounded like "I am" (standard for phone). Give me a "can-do" check for the phone intro.

Twists:

* The line is very bad (noise).
* You are calling the wrong number.
* You forget the name of the person you want.
* The person on the phone speaks very loudly.
* You have to leave a message (just your name and number).
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 004
Session Idea: Checking-Train-Destination: navigate 'Checking the Train Destination' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Checking the Train Destination
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request and understand warnings.
Context: You are on a train platform and want to make sure you are getting on the right train.
Correction: Helper will recast "This train [City]?" to "Is this the train to [City]?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 004.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Checking-Train-Destination: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Train" and destination cities.
Human steps:

* Say "Train" ten times.
* Say "To [City]" five times.
* Practice "Is this the train?" five times.
AI helper script: I am a passenger. You ask me "Train to [City]?" and I will say "Yes" or "No." Let's do ten different cities.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 004.2
Phase Idea: Model Checking-Train-Destination: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the confirmation question.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. Is this the train to the airport?"
* Helper responds: "Yes, it is." or "No, platform four."
* Listen for the word "Platform" and a number.
* Repeat "Platform four" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Show a "Ticket" to the helper. Ask the question. Use fingers to show the platform number. Speak very slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 004.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Checking-Train-Destination: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Confirm your train with a stranger.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper on the "platform."
* Ask if the train goes to your destination.
* Listen for "Yes" or a different platform number.
* Repeat the simulation, but the helper says "The train is late."
AI helper script: Act as a passenger. I will ask you about the train. Give me a "No" and point to a different direction. If I look confused, say the platform number again.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 004.4
Phase Idea: Polish Checking-Train-Destination: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the destination name.
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. Is this the train to [City]? Platform two? Thank you."
* Listen: Was the city name clear?
* Write "Platform" and a number in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Platform" to ensure the consonants are sharp. Give me a "can-do" check for the confirmation.

Twists:

* The train is leaving right now!
* You have the wrong platform.
* There are no trains today.
* The stranger doesn't know.
* You are on the train already and asking the conductor.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 005
Session Idea: Asking-Receipt: navigate 'Asking for a Receipt' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking for a Receipt
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request.
Context: You have just paid for an item in a shop and need a receipt for your records.
Correction: Helper will recast "Paper please" to "A receipt, please."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 005.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Receipt: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill the word "Receipt."
Human steps:

* Say "Receipt" ten times (focus on the 'silent p').
* Say "A receipt, please" five times.
* Practice "Thank you" after receiving it.
AI helper script: I am a cashier. You pretend to give me money, and then ask for a receipt. I will say "Here you go."

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 005.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Receipt: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the request at the end of a sale.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "That is ten dollars."
* Helper models: "Okay. A receipt, please?"
* Helper responds: "Yes, here it is."
* Repeat "A receipt, please" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the end of a transaction. 1. Pay. 2. Ask for receipt. 3. Take receipt. 4. Say goodbye. Use a piece of scrap paper as the receipt.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 005.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Receipt: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully get a receipt.
Human steps:

* Pretend to buy a coffee or a tool from the helper.
* Pay the "price."
* Ask clearly for the receipt.
* Repeat the simulation, but this time the machine is "broken."
AI helper script: Act as a shopkeeper. I will pay you. Wait for me to ask for the receipt. Once, say "No receipt today" to see how I react (e.g., "Oh, okay").

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 005.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Receipt: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the pronunciation of "Receipt."
Human steps:

* Record: "Ten dollars? Okay. A receipt, please. Thank you. Goodbye."
* Listen: Did you say the 'p' (you shouldn't!)?
* Write "Receipt" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Receipt" to make it sound natural (re-seet). Give me a "can-do" check for the request.

Twists:

* You need the receipt for "Work."
* The cashier is busy with another customer.
* You lost your receipt and are asking for a new one.
* The receipt is very long.
* You want the receipt in your "Email."
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 006
Session Idea: Asking-How-Do: navigate 'Asking "How Do You Say...?"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking "How Do You Say...?"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask simple questions and make requests for help.
Context: you see an object (like a tool or food) but you don't know the word in the target language.
Correction: Helper will recast "What is this?" to "How do you say this in [Language]?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 006.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-How-Do: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Automate the "learning" question.
Human steps:

* Say "How do you say this?" ten times.
* Point to objects and say "What is this?" five times.
* Practice "Please repeat" three times.
AI helper script: I will point to things in the room. You ask me "What is this?" and I will tell you the word. This is for speed and curiosity.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 006.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-How-Do: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the question used to bridge a language gap.
Human steps:

* Helper points to a pen and says: "How do you say this?"
* Helper responds: "A pen."
* Helper says: "A pen. Thank you."
* Repeat the full question "How do you say this in [Language]?" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction using five different objects. 1. Point. 2. Ask question. 3. Hear answer. 4. Repeat answer. 5. Say thank you. Speak slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 006.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-How-Do: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Learn three new words from the helper.
Human steps:

* Find three things in your room or on a screen.
* Ask the helper how to say each one.
* Repeat the word the helper gives you until it is clear.
* Repeat the simulation, but ask the helper to "Write it down" (pretend).
AI helper script: Act as a language helper. I will point at things. Give me the name of the object. If I say it wrong, recast it slowly. Ask me "Do you understand?"

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 006.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-How-Do: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Record the "Learning" phrase.
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. How do you say this? [New Word]? Thank you. Repeat, please."
* Listen: Was the question clear and polite?
* Write the three new words in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the question for better rhythm. Give me a "can-do" check for asking for help.

Twists:

* The helper doesn't know the word.
* The word is very long and difficult.
* You are asking about an action (e.g., "Running"), not an object.
* The helper speaks a different dialect.
* You want to know "How do you spell it?"
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 007
Session Idea: Asking-Specific-Vegetable: navigate 'Asking for a Specific Vegetable' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking for a Specific Vegetable
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request and understand numbers.
Context: You are at a village market and need to buy three onions.
Correction: Helper will recast "I onions" to "Onions, please" or "Three onions, please."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 007.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Specific-Vegetable: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill vegetable names and numbers 1-5.
Human steps:

* Say "Onion," "Potato," "Tomato" five times each.
* Say "One, two, three" five times.
* Practice "Three potatoes, please" five times.
AI helper script: I am a market vendor. I will say a vegetable. You say "Two [Vegetable], please" as fast as you can.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 007.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Specific-Vegetable: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Observe the quantity request.
Human steps:

* Helper points and says: "Hello. Tomatoes, please."
* Helper says: "How many?"
* Helper models: "Three, please."
* Repeat the quantities (One, Two, Three, Four, Five) after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the market scene. Use your hands to count the vegetables. Speak very slowly: "I want... four... onions."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 007.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Specific-Vegetable: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Buy a specific amount of food.
Human steps:

* Greet the helper and point to an imaginary vegetable.
* State the vegetable name and the number you want.
* Pay the price the helper gives you.
* Repeat the simulation, but the helper says they only have "One" left.
AI helper script: Act as a market vendor. I will buy vegetables. Ask me "How many?" and give me a price like "Two dollars." If I am unclear, point to the onions and ask "This?"

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 007.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Specific-Vegetable: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the number and noun combination.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. Three onions, please. How much? Two dollars? Okay, thank you."
* Listen: Did the 's' at the end of "onions" sound clear?
* Write your "Shopping list" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the plural 's' if I missed it. Give me a "can-do" check for the quantity request.

Twists:

* The onions are "small."
* You want a different color (Red or White).
* You don't have a bag.
* The vendor is shouting to other people.
* You change your mind and want potatoes instead.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 008
Session Idea: Asking-Where-Meeting: navigate 'Asking "Where is the Meeting?" at Work' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking "Where is the Meeting?" at Work
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions about a work location.
Context: You are at the office and are lost looking for the 10:00 meeting.
Correction: Helper will recast "Meeting where?" to "Excuse me, where is the meeting?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 008.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Where-Meeting: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill work locations and the "Meeting" word.
Human steps:

* Say "Meeting" ten times.
* Say "Office," "Room," and "Café" five times each.
* Say "Where is it?" five times.
AI helper script: I am a colleague. Every time you say "Meeting?", I will give you a room number. This is for number and location practice.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 008.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Where-Meeting: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the location question and answer.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. Where is the meeting?"
* Helper responds: "Room five." or "In the office."
* Listen for the prepositions "Room" or "In."
* Repeat "Room ten" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Show a "Calendar" on your phone. Ask the question. Use fingers to show the room number. Speak slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 008.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Where-Meeting: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Find the meeting room.
Human steps:

* Approach the "colleague" and ask for the meeting.
* Listen to the room number or location.
* Say "Thank you" and pretend to walk there.
* Repeat the simulation, but the colleague says "The meeting is tomorrow."
AI helper script: Act as a co-worker. I will ask for the meeting. Give me a room number (1-10) or say "In the café." If I look lost, point and say "Go left."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 008.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Where-Meeting: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "Where is" and the room number.
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. Where is the meeting today? Room four? Thank you. See you there."
* Listen: Did you sound professional?
* Write "Room [Number]" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Meeting" if the vowel sound was off. Give me a "can-do" check for finding the location.

Twists:

* You are ten minutes late.
* The room is changed to "Room 2."
* The colleague doesn't know about a meeting.
* You are in the wrong building.
* The meeting is "Online."
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 009
Session Idea: Understanding-Platform-Gate: navigate 'Understanding Platform and Gate Numbers' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Understanding Platform and Gate Numbers
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can understand very short instructions and numbers.
Context: You are at a busy airport or train station asking a guard for your gate.
Correction: Helper will recast "Where go?" to "Where is Gate [Number]?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 009.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Understanding-Platform-Gate: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Gate," "Platform," and numbers 1-20.
Human steps:

* Say "Gate" and "Platform" ten times each.
* Count from 1 to 20 slowly.
* Say "Where is Gate Five?" five times.
AI helper script: I am a station guard. You say a number, and I will say "Gate [Number]" or "Platform [Number]." This is to link the words with the numbers.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 009.2
Phase Idea: Model Understanding-Platform-Gate: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the directional response with numbers.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. Where is Platform Ten?"
* Helper points and says: "Platform Ten is over there."
* Helper says: "Gate Twelve? Go straight."
* Repeat the phrases "Over there" and "Go straight" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction with three different numbers. Use your whole arm to point. Speak slowly: "Gate... seven... is... left."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 009.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Understanding-Platform-Gate: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Find your gate before your flight/train leaves.
Human steps:

* Approach the "guard" and ask for a specific gate number.
* Listen to the direction and confirm it (e.g., "Straight?").
* Say "Thank you" and pretend to run to the gate.
* Repeat the simulation, but this time the gate has changed.
AI helper script: Act as a guard. I will ask for a gate. Give me a direction. Once, say "Gate changed! Go to Gate 20." Force me to listen to the new number.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 009.4
Phase Idea: Polish Understanding-Platform-Gate: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "Gate" vs "Platform."
Human steps:

* Record: "Where is Gate nine? Go straight? Okay, thank you. Goodbye."
* Listen: Was the number clear?
* Write "Gate" and "Platform" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Straight" if the 'str' sound was messy. Give me a "can-do" check for understanding the number.

Twists:

* You are at the "Bus" station, not the airport.
* You have many bags and are slow.
* The guard is talking on a radio.
* The sign says a different number.
* You need to find the "Exit."
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 010
Session Idea: Asking-Do-You: navigate 'Asking "Do You Take Credit Cards?"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking "Do You Take Credit Cards?"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request and understand a simple answer.
Context: You are in a small village shop or a cafe and only have a card, no cash.
Correction: Helper will recast "Card okay?" to "Do you take credit cards?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 010.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Do-You: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Card" and "Cash."
Human steps:

* Say "Credit card" ten times.
* Say "Cash" ten times.
* Say "Do you take cards?" five times.
AI helper script: I am a shop owner. You show me a card and ask the question. I will say "Yes" or "No, only cash." We will repeat this until the question is fast.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 010.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Do-You: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the payment choice dialogue.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "That is five dollars."
* Helper models: "Do you take credit cards?"
* Helper responds: "Yes, we do." or "No, cash only."
* Repeat the response "Cash only" three times.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Point to an imaginary card machine or a cash box. Speak very slowly: "No... card. Only... cash."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 010.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Do-You: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Check the payment method before buying.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper with an item.
* Ask "How much?"
* Before paying, ask "Do you take credit cards?"
* If the answer is "No," say "Oh, sorry" and pretend to leave.
AI helper script: Act as a shopkeeper. I will ask the card question. Give me a "No" half of the time. If I say "No," ask "Do you have cash?" to see my response.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 010.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Do-You: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "Do you" question starter.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. How much? Five dollars? Do you take credit cards? No? Okay, sorry. Thank you."
* Listen: Did you sound like a question?
* Write "Card" and "Cash" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Credit card" for clarity. Give me a "can-do" check for the payment question.

Twists:

* The machine is "Broken."
* You want to pay with your "Phone."
* There is an ATM nearby.
* You have "No cash."
* The shop has a "Minimum" for cards (e.g., $10).
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 011
Session Idea: Inviting-Someone-Coffee: navigate 'Inviting Someone for a Coffee' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Inviting Someone for a Coffee
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can say simple greetings and make very simple requests/invitations.
Context: You are talking to a new neighbor or colleague and want to be friendly.
Correction: Helper will recast "We coffee?" to "Would you like a coffee?" or "Coffee today?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 011.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Inviting-Someone-Coffee: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Automate the invitation phrase.
Human steps:

* Say "Coffee?" ten times with a questioning tone.
* Say "Would you like a coffee?" five times.
* Practice "Today?" and "Tomorrow?" three times each.
AI helper script: I am a friend. Every time you say "Coffee?", I will say "Yes, please!" or "I am busy." This is for speed and social comfort.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 011.2
Phase Idea: Model Inviting-Someone-Coffee: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the invitation and the time setting.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Hi! How are you?"
* Helper models: "Would you like a coffee today?"
* Helper responds: "Yes! What time?"
* Helper says: "Three o'clock?"
* Repeat "Three o'clock?" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model a friendly invitation. 1. Greet. 2. Invite. 3. Set a time. 4. Say "See you later." Speak slowly and use your hand to show drinking coffee.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 011.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Inviting-Someone-Coffee: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully invite someone to coffee.
Human steps:

* Greet the helper and ask them if they want coffee.
* If they say yes, suggest a time (e.g., "Ten o'clock?").
* Say "Great! See you later."
* Repeat the simulation, but suggest "Tea" instead of coffee.
AI helper script: Act as a colleague. I will invite you. Say "Yes" and ask me "What time?" If I am too quiet, ask me to repeat the time.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 011.4
Phase Idea: Polish Inviting-Someone-Coffee: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "Would you like" structure.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hi. Would you like a coffee tomorrow? Two o'clock? Great. See you later."
* Listen: Did you sound friendly and inviting?
* Write "Coffee" and "Tomorrow" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Coffee" for the 'ee' sound. Give me a "can-do" check for the social invitation.

Twists:

* You want to go "Now."
* The helper says "No, thank you."
* You want a "Beer," not a coffee.
* You are in a rush.
* You have to pay (e.g., "My treat").
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 012
Session Idea: Saying-I-Like: navigate 'Saying "I Like This" or "I Don't Like This"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Saying "I Like This" or "I Don't Like This"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions about preferences.
Context: You are at a dinner or a shop and are giving your opinion on a food or item.
Correction: Helper will recast "This no good" to "I don't like this."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 012.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Saying-I-Like: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "I like" and "I don't like."
Human steps:

* Say "I like this" ten times with a smile.
* Say "I don't like this" ten times with a serious face.
* Practice "Do you like it?" five times.
AI helper script: I will name a food (Apple, Fish, Coffee). You say "I like it" or "I don't like it" as fast as you can.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 012.2
Phase Idea: Model Saying-I-Like: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear opinions shared in a social setting.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "The soup is very good. I like it."
* Helper says: "The tea is cold. I don't like it."
* Listen for the words "Very good" and "Cold."
* Repeat "I don't like it" after the helper models a bad food.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Point to an imaginary plate. 1. Eat. 2. Give opinion. 3. Ask partner. Speak slowly and use clear facial expressions.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 012.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Saying-I-Like: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Share your preferences with the helper.
Human steps:

* Pretend to eat three different things with the helper.
* State clearly if you like or don't like each one.
* Ask the helper "And you? Do you like it?"
* Repeat the simulation, but use the phrases for "Music" or "Weather."
AI helper script: Act as a friend at lunch. I will tell you what I think. Ask me "Do you like [Food]?" and listen to my answer. If I say "It's okay," try to understand the tone.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 012.4
Phase Idea: Polish Saying-I-Like: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "don't" contraction.
Human steps:

* Record: "The coffee is good. I like it. The bread is old. I don't like it. Thank you."
* Listen: Did you say "don't" clearly?
* Write "I like" and "I don't like" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the sentences for better emotion in the voice. Give me a "can-do" check for stating preferences.

Twists:

* You "love" it (very much).
* You are trying to be polite about something you hate.
* The food is "spicy."
* You want "more."
* The helper asks "Why?"
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 013
Session Idea: Asking-Can-You: navigate 'Asking "Can You Help Me?" to a Colleague' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking "Can You Help Me?" to a Colleague
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request for assistance.
Context: You are at work and a box is too heavy or a machine is not working.
Correction: Helper will recast "Help box" to "Can you help me with this box?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 013.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Can-You: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Help" and "Please."
Human steps:

* Say "Help" ten times.
* Say "Can you help me?" ten times.
* Say "It is heavy" or "It is broken" five times.
AI helper script: I am your colleague. Every time you say "Help!", I will walk over to you. Then you point and say what is wrong.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 013.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Can-You: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the request and the reason.
Human steps:

* Helper points to a heavy box and says: "Excuse me. Can you help me?"
* Helper says: "This is very heavy."
* Helper responds: "Yes, of course."
* Repeat "This is very heavy" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Look stressed. 2. Ask for help. 3. Point to the problem. 4. Say thank you. Speak very slowly and pretend to lift something heavy.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 013.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Can-You: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully get help at work.
Human steps:

* Approach the "colleague" and use a polite opener.
* Ask for help with an imaginary task (e.g., a door, a box, a computer).
* Explain why you need help (e.g., "I don't know" or "It is big").
* Say "Thank you" when they help.
AI helper script: Act as a co-worker. I will ask for help. Give me a "Yes" and ask "What is the problem?" If I just say "Help," wait for me to explain more.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 013.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Can-You: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "Can you."
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me, Sam. Can you help me? This is very heavy. Thank you for your help."
* Listen: Was the request polite?
* Write "Heavy" and "Broken" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Help" to ensure the 'p' is heard. Give me a "can-do" check for the request.

Twists:

* The colleague is on the phone.
* The box is "Very, very" heavy.
* You need two people to help.
* The colleague says "One moment."
* You find out you can do it yourself after all.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 014
Session Idea: Asking-Next-Bus: navigate 'Asking for the "Next Bus" Time' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking for the "Next Bus" Time
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask simple questions about a schedule.
Context: You are at a village bus stop and want to know when the bus arrives.
Correction: Helper will recast "When next?" to "When is the next bus?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 014.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Next-Bus: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Next" and "Bus."
Human steps:

* Say "Next bus" ten times.
* Say "What time?" five times.
* Say "Ten minutes" or "Five minutes" three times.
AI helper script: I am a person waiting for the bus. You ask "When?" and I will give you a time. This is for time and number practice.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 014.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Next-Bus: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the question and the time response.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. When is the next bus?"
* Helper responds: "In ten minutes."
* Helper says: "Thank you. Is it late?"
* Repeat "In ten minutes" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Point to your watch. Speak slowly: "The... next... bus... is... at... four... o'clock."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 014.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Next-Bus: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Find out the bus time from a stranger.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper and ask for the next bus time.
* Listen to the number and repeat it to confirm (e.g., "Five minutes?").
* Say "Thank you" and wait.
* Repeat the simulation, but the helper says "No more buses today."
AI helper script: Act as a passenger. I will ask you about the bus. Give me a time like "Ten thirty." Once, say "The bus is finished" to see how I react.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 014.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Next-Bus: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "When is."
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. When is the next bus to the city? Ten minutes? Okay, thank you."
* Listen: Did the question sound clear?
* Write "Next" and "Bus" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Next" if the 'xt' was missing. Give me a "can-do" check for the schedule question.

Twists:

* You are at the wrong stop.
* The bus is "Late."
* You need the "Last" bus, not the next one.
* The stranger is looking at a phone app.
* It starts raining while you wait.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 015
Session Idea: Buying-Bottle-Water: navigate 'Buying a Bottle of Water' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Buying a Bottle of Water
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can order a simple item and handle money.
Context: You are in a small city kiosk or shop and are very thirsty.
Correction: Helper will recast "Water me" to "A bottle of water, please."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 015.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Buying-Bottle-Water: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Water" and "Bottle."
Human steps:

* Say "Water" ten times.
* Say "A bottle of water, please" five times.
* Say "How much is it?" five times.
AI helper script: I am a shopkeeper. You pretend to pick up a bottle and ask the price. I will give you a price like "One dollar."

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 015.2
Phase Idea: Model Buying-Bottle-Water: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the simple purchase sequence.
Human steps:

* Helper points and says: "Hello. Water, please."
* Helper says: "Small or large?"
* Helper models: "Small, please. How much?"
* Repeat the words "Small" and "Large" five times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the purchase. 1. Greet. 2. Request water. 3. Choose size. 4. Pay. 5. Say thank you. Use your hands to show sizes. Speak slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 015.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Buying-Bottle-Water: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully buy a drink.
Human steps:

* Greet the helper and request the water.
* Choose a size when asked.
* Pay the price the helper gives you.
* Repeat the simulation, but change the item to "Juice."
AI helper script: Act as a shopkeeper. I will buy water. Ask me "Cold or warm?" to see if I understand the extra choice. Give me a price with cents (e.g., "One fifty").

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 015.4
Phase Idea: Polish Buying-Bottle-Water: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "of" in "Bottle of water."
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. One bottle of water, please. Cold? Yes. How much? Thank you."
* Listen: Did you say "of" or did you skip it?
* Write "Water" and "Bottle" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Water" for the 't' or 'd' sound depending on the target language. Give me a "can-do" check for the purchase.

Twists:

* There is no cold water.
* You want "Two" bottles.
* The shop is out of water.
* You have no coins.
* The water is "Sparkling" (with gas).
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Correction: Helper will recast "Go now" to "Goodbye! See you tomorrow."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 016.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Saying-Goodbye-Colleague: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Automate closing greetings.
Human steps:

* Say "Goodbye" ten times.
* Say "See you tomorrow" ten times.
* Say "Have a nice evening" five times.
AI helper script: I am your boss. Every time you walk past me and say "Goodbye," I will say it back. Let's do it for five different "days."

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 016.2
Phase Idea: Model Saying-Goodbye-Colleague: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the sequence of leaving.
Human steps:

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 016.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Saying-Goodbye-Colleague: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Say goodbye to the helper professionally.
Human steps:

* Pretend you are finished with work.
* Walk up to the helper and say "I am going now. Goodbye."
* Respond when they say "See you tomorrow."
* Repeat the simulation, but say "See you on Monday" (for the weekend).
AI helper script: Act as a co-worker. I will leave. Greet me back. If I say "Monday," ask me "Do you have plans?" to see if I can say one simple thing (e.g., "Rest").

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 016.4
Phase Idea: Polish Saying-Goodbye-Colleague: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "See you."
Human steps:

* Record: "Goodbye, everyone. I am going now. See you tomorrow. Have a nice night."
* Listen: Did you sound happy and clear?
* Write "See you tomorrow" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Tomorrow" for the 'r' sounds. Give me a "can-do" check for the closing greeting.

Twists:

* You are leaving early.
* You won't be here tomorrow.
* You are very tired.
* It is raining outside.
* You forgot your keys.

Session ID: 017
Session Idea: Asking-Time-Half: navigate 'Asking for the Time (Half-Past)' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking for the Time (Half-Past)
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions about the time.
Context: You are at a town square and your watch has stopped.
Correction: Helper will recast "Time?" to "What time is it?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 017.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Time-Half: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill numbers and the phrase "Half-past."
Human steps:

* Say "What time is it?" ten times.
* Say "Eight-thirty," "Nine-thirty," "Ten-thirty."
* Practice "Half-past" three times.
AI helper script: I will show you a "time" with my hands (e.g., 2:30). You say the time as fast as you can.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 017.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Time-Half: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the time question and the "Half-past" answer.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. Do you have the time?"
* Helper responds: "Yes, it is half-past four."
* Helper models: "Four-thirty?" "Yes, four-thirty."
* Repeat "Half-past" five times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Point to an imaginary clock. Speak slowly: "It... is... half... past... two."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 017.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Time-Half: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully get the time from the helper.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper and ask "What time is it?"
* Listen to the answer (focus on the '30' or 'half-past').
* Repeat the time to confirm it.
* Say "Thank you" and pretend to adjust your watch.
AI helper script: Act as a stranger. I will ask the time. Give me an answer like "Six-thirty." If I look confused, say "Six... and... thirty."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 017.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Time-Half: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the number 30.
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me, what is the time? Five-thirty? Okay, thank you. Have a nice day."
* Listen: Was the "thirty" clear (not 'thirteen')?
* Write "Half-past" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Thirty" if it sounded like 'Thirteen.' Give me a "can-do" check for the time question.

Twists:

* The stranger's watch is broken too.
* It is "Almost" six o'clock.
* You are very late for a bus.
* The stranger speaks very quickly.
* You need the time in "Military" (24-hour) format.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 018
Session Idea: Saying-I-Am: navigate 'Saying "I Am Busy Now" at Work' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Saying "I Am Busy Now" at Work
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions and give short instructions.
Context: You are at your desk or workstation and a colleague wants to talk, but you have a deadline.
Correction: Helper will recast "No talk" to "I am busy now" or "Maybe later."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 018.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Saying-I-Am: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Busy" and "Later."
Human steps:

* Say "I am busy" ten times.
* Say "Maybe later" ten times.
* Say "I have work" five times.
AI helper script: I am a distracting colleague. Every time I say "Hey! Look at this!", you say "Sorry, I am busy now." We will do this fast to build your confidence in saying no.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 018.2
Phase Idea: Model Saying-I-Am: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the polite "Busy" response.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Hi! Do you have a minute?"
* Helper models: "Sorry, I am very busy now."
* Helper responds: "Oh, okay. When are you free?"
* Helper says: "Later? At four o'clock?"
* Repeat "Maybe later" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Approach desk. 2. Greet. 3. Hear "Busy." 4. Offer a later time. 5. Agree. Speak slowly and look at an imaginary computer.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 018.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Saying-I-Am: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully manage your work time.
Human steps:

* Pretend to work on a task.
* When the helper interrupts, say you are busy.
* Suggest a later time (e.g., "In one hour" or "At three").
* Repeat the simulation, but this time the helper is your "Boss."
AI helper script: Act as a co-worker. I will try to talk to you. When you say you are busy, ask "Is it the report?" to see if you can give a one-word answer (e.g., "Yes").

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 018.4
Phase Idea: Polish Saying-I-Am: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "I am [Adjective]."
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. Sorry, I am busy now. I have work. Maybe later? Thank you."
* Listen: Did you sound polite but firm?
* Write "Busy" and "Later" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Busy" for the 'z' sound. Give me a "can-do" check for the work boundary.

Twists:

* The colleague has a "small" question.
* You are busy "all day."
* The colleague is your friend and you want to talk.
* Your computer is "broken" and that's why you are busy.
* You are hungry and "busy" eating lunch.

Session ID: 019
Session Idea: Identifying-Seat-Number: navigate 'Identifying Your Seat Number' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Identifying Your Seat Number
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can give and ask for basic information and numbers.
Context: You are on a bus or train and someone is sitting in your seat.
Correction: Helper will recast "My chair" to "Excuse me, I think this is my seat."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 019.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Identifying-Seat-Number: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Seat" and numbers 1-50.
Human steps:

* Say "Seat" ten times.
* Say "Seat number ten," "Seat number twenty."
* Say "My seat, please" five times.
AI helper script: I am a passenger. You show me a ticket and say a number. I will say "Oh, sorry!" and move. Let's do this for five different seat numbers.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 019.2
Phase Idea: Model Identifying-Seat-Number: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the polite confrontation about a seat.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. I think this is my seat."
* Helper points to ticket and says: "Number fifteen."
* Helper responds: "Oh, sorry! My mistake."
* Repeat "I think this is my seat" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Walk to seat. 2. See person. 3. Check ticket. 4. Speak politely. 5. Show ticket. Speak slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 019.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Identifying-Seat-Number: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Get your correct seat.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper who is sitting in your "seat."
* State your seat number clearly.
* Show your "ticket" (imaginary).
* Repeat the simulation, but the person says "No, this is my seat." (Check your ticket again!).
AI helper script: Act as a passenger. I will sit in your seat. When you tell me, say "Are you sure?" to make me check my ticket. Once, move immediately.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 019.4
Phase Idea: Polish Identifying-Seat-Number: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "I think."
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. I think this is my seat. Number ten? See? Thank you."
* Listen: Was the number clear?
* Write "Seat" and your favorite number in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Seat" to ensure the 'ea' is long. Give me a "can-do" check for the seat confirmation.

Twists:

* You are in the wrong "Carriage" (Train part).
* The seat is "Dirty."
* You want to change seats with the person.
* The person is sleeping.
* There are no numbers on the seats.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 020
Session Idea: Asking-Bag-Please: navigate 'Asking for a "Bag, Please"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking for a "Bag, Please"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request.
Context: You are at a grocery store in the city and have too many items to carry.
Correction: Helper will recast "Give plastic" to "A bag, please."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 020.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Bag-Please: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Bag" and "Plastic."
Human steps:

* Say "Bag" ten times.
* Say "A bag, please" ten times.
* Say "Two bags, please" five times.
AI helper script: I am a cashier. Every time you finish "paying," you ask for a bag. I will say "Large or small?"

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 020.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Bag-Please: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the request for a bag and the size choice.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "That is twenty dollars."
* Helper models: "A bag, please?"
* Helper says: "Paper or plastic?"
* Helper responds: "Plastic, please. Thank you."
* Repeat "Paper or plastic?" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Use two hands to show a big bag and a small bag. Speak slowly: "Do... you... want... a... bag?"

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 020.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Bag-Please: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully get a bag for your items.
Human steps:

* Pretend to buy many items from the helper.
* When they finish "scanning," ask for a bag.
* Choose a material (Paper/Plastic) or size (Small/Large).
* Repeat the simulation, but the helper says "Bags are ten cents."
AI helper script: Act as a cashier. I will buy things. Wait for me to ask for the bag. Tell me "Ten cents" to see if I say "Okay" or "No."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 020.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Bag-Please: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "p" in "Plastic."
Human steps:

* Record: "A bag, please. Plastic is okay. How much? Ten cents? Okay. Thank you."
* Listen: Did you sound polite?
* Write "Bag" and "Plastic" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Plastic" to ensure the 'p' and 'l' are distinct. Give me a "can-do" check for the request.

Twists:

* You have your own bag (Say "No, thank you").
* The bag "breaks."
* You need a "Big" bag for a box.
* The cashier is very fast.
* You want "Three" bags.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 021
Session Idea: Asking-What-Phone: navigate 'Asking "What is Your Phone Number?"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking "What is Your Phone Number?"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions and understand numbers.
Context: You are meeting a new friend in a village and want to stay in touch.
Correction: Helper will recast "Give phone" to "What is your phone number?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 021.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-What-Phone: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill numbers 0-9 and the word "Phone."
Human steps:

* Say "Phone number" ten times.
* Count from 0 to 9 five times.
* Say "What is your number?" five times.
AI helper script: I will say a number. You repeat it. Then I will say a "fake" phone number, and you try to repeat all seven digits.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 021.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-What-Phone: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the request for a number and the digit-by-digit response.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "You are very nice. What is your phone number?"
* Helper responds: "It is five-five-five... zero-one-two-three."
* Helper says: "Wait. Five-five-five... zero-one-two-three. Okay."
* Repeat the numbers after the helper models them.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Be friendly. 2. Ask for the number. 3. Listen. 4. Repeat it back to check. Speak very slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 021.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-What-Phone: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Exchange phone numbers with the helper.
Human steps:

* Tell the helper your "number" (can be fake).
* Ask the helper for their number.
* Repeat the number they give you to make sure you got it.
* Say "Thank you. I will call you."
AI helper script: Act as a new friend. I will ask for your number. Then I will give you my number (use different digits each time). If I go too fast, say "Slowly, please."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 021.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-What-Phone: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the number "Zero."
Human steps:

* Record: "What is your phone number? Five-zero-nine... two-one? Okay, thank you. See you later."
* Listen: Was the "zero" clear?
* Write your fake number in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast any numbers that were confusing (e.g., 'five' and 'nine' sometimes sound similar). Give me a "can-do" check for the information exchange.

Twists:

* You don't have a phone.
* The friend's number is "Very long."
* You forget one number.
* You are at a loud party.
* You want to "Text," not call.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 022
Session Idea: Stating-I-Am: navigate 'Stating "I Am Hungry" (Daily Life)' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Stating "I Am Hungry" (Daily Life)
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions about myself.
Context: You are with a friend or spouse in a city and need to find food.
Correction: Helper will recast "Food want" to "I am hungry" or "Let's eat."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 022.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Stating-I-Am: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Hungry" and "Thirsty."
Human steps:

* Say "I am hungry" ten times with a hand on your stomach.
* Say "I am thirsty" ten times.
* Say "Where is a restaurant?" five times.
AI helper script: I am your friend. Every time you say "I am hungry," I will point to a different place (e.g., "Café," "Market," "Pizza").

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 022.2
Phase Idea: Model Stating-I-Am: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the statement of need and the suggestion.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "I am hungry. Are you hungry?"
* Helper responds: "Yes, very hungry. Let's eat."
* Helper says: "Is there a café here?"
* Repeat "Let's eat" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Act tired/hungry. 2. State the problem. 3. Ask a question. 4. Move to find food. Speak very slowly and use gestures.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 022.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Stating-I-Am: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Communicate your hunger and find a place to eat.
Human steps:

* Tell the helper you are hungry.
* Ask them if they are hungry too.
* Suggest a place (e.g., "The market?").
* Repeat the simulation, but say you are "Thirsty" and want "Water."
AI helper script: Act as a friend. I will tell you I am hungry. Ask me "What do you want?" and "Where is it?" If I just point, ask for the word.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 022.4
Phase Idea: Polish Stating-I-Am: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "I am [Adjective]."
Human steps:

* Record: "I am hungry. Are you hungry? Let's eat at the café. Is it far? No? Okay."
* Listen: Did you sound natural?
* Write "Hungry" and "Thirsty" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Hungry" for the 'h' and 'ng' sounds. Give me a "can-do" check for stating your needs.

Twists:

* You are "Very, very" hungry.
* Everything is "Closed."
* You have no money for food.
* You only want "Bread."
* The friend is not hungry.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Purpose: Drill work equipment and "Broken."

* Say "Printer" ten times.
* Say "It is broken" ten times.
* Say "Not working" five times.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 023.2
Phase Idea: Model Stating-Printer-Broken: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the problem statement and the call for help.

* Helper points to a machine and says: "Excuse me. The printer is broken."
* Helper says: "It is not working. Can you help?"
* Helper responds: "Yes. Let me see."

* Explain the problem simply (e.g., "Red light" or "No paper").
* Ask them to "Look, please."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus

Minutes: 10

Human steps:

* Listen: Was the word "Broken" clear?
* Write "Printer" and "Broken" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Printer" to ensure the 'er' sound is clear. Give me a "can-do" check for reporting the issue.

Twists:

* You just need to "Plug it in."
* There is a lot of smoke! (Emergency).
* You are in a rush to print a report.
* The boss is angry that it is broken.
* You fix it yourself (Say "It's okay now!").

Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 024.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-How-Far: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Far" and "Near."
Human steps:

* Say "How far is it?" ten times.
* Say "Is it near?" five times.
* Say "Five minutes" or "One hour" three times each.
AI helper script: I will point to a place (e.g., The moon, The door, The city). You say "Far" or "Near" as fast as you can.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 024.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-How-Far: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the distance question and the time response.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Excuse me. Where is the museum?"
* Helper says: "It is over there. Go left."
* Helper models: "How far is it? Is it far?"
* Helper responds: "No, it is near. Two minutes."
* Repeat "Is it far?" after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Use your hands to show a long distance and a short distance. Speak slowly: "The... hospital... is... very... far."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output

Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-How-Far: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Determine if you should walk or take a bus.
Human steps:

* Ask the helper for a location (e.g., "The bank?").
* When they point, ask "How far is it?"
* Decide "Okay, I walk" or "No, I take a bus" based on their answer.
* Repeat the simulation, but the helper says it is "Ten kilometers."
AI helper script: Act as a local person. I will ask for directions. Tell me "It is near" or "It is very far." If I ask "How far?", give me a number of minutes.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 024.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-How-Far: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "How far."
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. Where is the park? Is it far? Ten minutes? Okay, I walk. Thank you."
* Listen: Did you sound like a traveler?
* Write "Far" and "Near" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Far" to ensure the 'f' and 'r' are distinct. Give me a "can-do" check for the distance question.

Twists:

* You are very tired.
* It is dark outside.
* You have a map but it is confusing.
* The person says "I don't know."
* The place is "Behind" you.

Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions and give short instructions.
Context: You have finished a task in a workshop or kitchen and want to tell your supervisor.
Correction: Helper will recast "Work done" to "I am finished" or "I am done."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 028.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Stating-I-M: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Finished" and "Done."
Human steps:

* Say "I am finished" ten times.
* Say "I am done" ten times.
* Say "What is next?" five times.
AI helper script: I am your boss. Every time you finish an "imaginary" job (like cleaning), you come to me and say the phrase. I will say "Good job!"

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 028.2
Phase Idea: Model Stating-I-M: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the "Task complete" dialogue.
Human steps:

* Helper finishes a task and walks to supervisor.
* Helper models: "Hello. I am finished now."
* Helper says: "Good. Please wait here."
* Helper responds: "Okay. What is the next task?"
* Repeat "What is the next task?" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Clean table. 2. Stand up. 3. Greet supervisor. 4. State "Finished." 5. Ask for new work. Speak slowly and look at your hands.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 028.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Stating-I-M: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Inform the helper that your work is complete.
Human steps:

* Pretend to finish a work task.
* Walk to the helper and state clearly that you are done.
* Ask "Is there more work?" or "What is next?"
* Repeat the simulation, but say you are "Going home" now.
AI helper script: Act as a supervisor. I will tell you I am done. Ask me "Did you finish the floor?" to see if I can say "Yes, I did."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 028.4
Phase Idea: Polish Stating-I-M: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "ed" sound (or equivalent).
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. I am finished with the box. What is next? Okay. Thank you. See you later."
* Listen: Did you sound professional and proactive?
* Write "Finished" and "Next" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Finished" to ensure the end of the word is sharp. Give me a "can-do" check for the work status update.

Twists:

* You are "Not" finished yet.
* You need "Ten more minutes."
* The task was "Easy."
* You are tired.
* The supervisor is busy.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

BEGIN PERFECT HOUR SESSION
Session ID: 029
Session Idea: Taxi-Stop-Here: navigate 'Taxi: "Stop Here, Please"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Taxi: "Stop Here, Please"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can give very short instructions.
Context: You are in a taxi in a city and have reached your destination.
Correction: Helper will recast "Here stop" to "Please stop here" or "Stop at the corner."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 029.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Taxi-Stop-Here: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Stop" and "Here."
Human steps:

* Say "Stop here, please" ten times.
* Say "At the corner" five times.
* Say "Left" and "Right" five times each.
AI helper script: I am a taxi driver. I will "drive" and you tell me where to go (Left, Right, Stop). I will follow your commands.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 029.2
Phase Idea: Model Taxi-Stop-Here: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the arrival and payment sequence.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Please stop here. At the red house."
* Helper says: "How much is it?"
* Helper responds: "Ten dollars."
* Helper says: "Here you go. Thank you. Goodbye."
* Repeat "Stop here, please" after the helper models it.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Sit in back seat. 2. Point to the house. 3. Give stop instruction. 4. Ask price. 5. Pay. Speak slowly.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 029.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Taxi-Stop-Here: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully end your taxi ride.
Human steps:

* Tell the "driver" (the helper) to stop at a specific place (e.g., "The hotel" or "The corner").
* Ask for the price.
* Pretend to pay and say "Keep the change" (just for fun).
* Repeat the simulation, but tell them to "Wait here, please."
AI helper script: Act as a taxi driver. I will give you instructions. Ask me "Here or there?" to force me to be specific. Give me a price like "Twelve fifty."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 029.4
Phase Idea: Polish Taxi-Stop-Here: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on "Please" at the start or end.
Human steps:

* Record: "Stop here, please. At the corner. How much? Ten dollars? Okay. Thank you. Goodbye."
* Listen: Did you sound clear while the car was "moving"?
* Write "Stop" and "Corner" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Corner" for the 'r' sounds. Give me a "can-do" check for the transport instruction.

Twists:

* You are at the "Wrong" house.
* You have no cash (Card?).
* You want the driver to "Wait" five minutes.
* The driver is going too fast.
* You have a lot of bags in the "Trunk" (Back).
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Session ID: 030
Session Idea: Asking-Menu-Please: navigate 'Asking for a "Menu, Please"' with a calm opener, one key question, and a clear next step.

Title: Asking for a "Menu, Please"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can make a very simple request.
Context: You have just sat down in a village restaurant and don't have a menu yet.
Correction: Helper will recast "Book please" to "The menu, please."

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 030.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-Menu-Please: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill "Menu" and "Drink."
Human steps:

* Say "Menu" ten times.
* Say "The menu, please" ten times.
* Say "What is good?" three times.
AI helper script: I am a waiter. You sit down and ask for the menu. I will say "One moment." Repeat this for five different "tables."

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 030.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-Menu-Please: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the request and the initial order.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Hello. Welcome."
* Helper models: "Hello. The menu, please?"
* Helper says: "Here is the menu. What drink?"
* Helper responds: "Water, please. Thank you."
* Repeat "The menu, please" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. 1. Sit down. 2. Greet waiter. 3. Ask for menu. 4. Order a drink. 5. Look at the menu. Speak very slowly and pretend to hold a large menu.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 030.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-Menu-Please: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Successfully start your meal.
Human steps:

* Sit with the helper and greet them.
* Ask for the menu clearly.
* Order one simple drink (e.g., "Tea").
* Repeat the simulation, but ask for the menu in "English" (or another language).
AI helper script: Act as a waiter. I will ask for the menu. Give it to me and ask "Are you ready to eat?" to see if I can say "No, one moment."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 030.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-Menu-Please: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "u" in "Menu."
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. The menu, please. Thank you. And a water. Is there a toilet here? Okay."
* Listen: Was the request polite?
* Write "Menu" and "Drink" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Menu" to ensure it doesn't sound like 'Man.' Give me a "can-do" check for the restaurant request.

Twists:

* There is "No" menu (The waiter says the food).
* You want a "Small" menu.
* The menu is on the "Wall."
* You need a "Table for two."
* You are very thirsty and ask for the drink first.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

Title: Asking "What is Your Name?"
Level: A1 (ACTFL Novice Low–Mid; CLB 1–2)
Partner: Human or AI
Goal (CLB): I can ask and answer simple questions about myself.
Context: You are at a community gathering and want to meet the person next to you.
Correction: Helper will recast "You name?" to "What is your name?"

PHASE 1
Name: Fluency loop
Phase ID: 031.1
Phase Idea: Rapid anchors for Asking-What-Name: build fast access to the core phrases.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Drill the question and the response.
Human steps:

* Say "What is your name?" ten times.
* Say "My name is [Your Name]" ten times.
* Practice "And you?" five times.
AI helper script: I will say a name. You ask "What is your name?" and I will respond. Then you say your own name.

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 031.2
Phase Idea: Model Asking-What-Name: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Minutes: 25
Purpose: Hear the name exchange sequence.
Human steps:

* Helper says: "Hello. My name is Sam. What is your name?"
* Helper responds: "My name is [Your Name]."
* Helper says: "Nice to meet you, [Your Name]."
* Repeat "What is your name?" three times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Greet, state name, ask name. Speak very slowly and gesture to yourself and the learner.

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 031.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Asking-What-Name: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Exchange names naturally.
Human steps:

* Approach the helper and say "Hello."
* Ask the helper for their name.
* Respond with your name when asked.
* Repeat the simulation, but pretend you didn't hear and say "Sorry?"
AI helper script: Act as a new neighbor. I will meet you. Ask me my name. If I speak too fast, say "Slowly, please."

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 031.4
Phase Idea: Polish Asking-What-Name: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "is" in the question.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. What is your name? My name is [Name]. Nice to meet you."
* Listen: Was the "is" clear in the question?
* Write "What is your name?" in your notebook.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the question for better clarity. Give me a "can-do" check for the social interaction.

Twists:

* You forget how to say your own name for a second.
* The person has a very long name.
* It is very noisy.
* You are meeting a famous person.
* You want to spell your name.
END PERFECT HOUR SESSION

* Say "I have a question" ten times.
* Practice raising your hand while speaking.
AI helper script: I am a teacher talking about a topic. Every time you say "Excuse me, I have a question," I will stop and say "Yes?"

PHASE 2
Name: Model and input
Phase ID: 032.2
Phase Idea: Model Stating-I-Have: hear a natural mini-dialogue and notice useful connectors.

Purpose: Hear the polite interruption.

* Helper models: "Excuse me. I have a question."

Name: Simulation output

Phase Idea: Role-play Stating-I-Have: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15

* Interrupt the helper using the practiced phrase.
* Ask one simple word (e.g., "Price?" or "Time?").
* Repeat the simulation with a different topic.
AI helper script: Act as a supervisor giving instructions. I will talk continuously. Stop me and ask your question. I will respond and then continue.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus

Phase Idea: Polish Stating-I-Have: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "h" sound in "Have."
Human steps:

* Record: "Excuse me. I have a question. What time? Thank you."
* Listen: Was the "h" in "have" audible?
* Write "I have a question" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast the word "Question" for the 'qu' sound. Give me a "can-do" check for the interruption.

Twists:

* You have "Two" questions.
* You are in a very large room.
* The speaker is a boss.
* You forget your question.
* The speaker says "One moment" (wait).

Twists:

* The sign is broken.

Purpose: Hear the possessive and identifying phrases.
Human steps:

* Helper points to a photo and says: "This is my mother."
* Helper points and says: "She is a teacher."
* Helper points and says: "This is my brother, Sam."
* Repeat "This is my..." five times after the helper.
AI helper script: Model the interaction. Point to imaginary people. Speak slowly: "This... is... my... sister... Maria."

PHASE 3
Name: Simulation output
Phase ID: 037.3
Phase Idea: Role-play Identifying-Family-Members: sustain the conversation and practice repair strategies.

Minutes: 15
Purpose: Introduce your family to the helper.
Human steps:

* Use your hands to show an imaginary photo.
* Introduce three family members to the helper.
* State their names simply (e.g., "This is my brother, John").
* Repeat the simulation, but introduce your "Son" or "Daughter."
AI helper script: Act as a colleague. I will look at your "photo." Ask me "What is his name?" or "Where is she?" to see if I can respond.

PHASE 4
Name: Record and focus
Phase ID: 037.4
Phase Idea: Polish Identifying-Family-Members: record a short recap and tighten the correction focus.

Minutes: 10
Purpose: Focus on the "is" vs "my" sequence.
Human steps:

* Record: "Hello. This is my mother. Her name is Mary. This is my brother. He is ten. Thank you."
* Listen: Did you use "is my" in the right order?
* Write "Mother" and "Father" in your log.
AI helper script: Listen to the recording. Recast "Brother" for the 'th' sound. Give me a "can-do" check for the identification.

Twists:

* You have a large family (many brothers).
* The photo is old.
* You forget the word for "Cousin."
* The colleague asks "Where are they?"
* You have a pet in the photo (This is my dog).
